          <a href="/wiki/Standard_state" title="Standard state">
           standard state
          </a>
          (at 25 °C [77 °F], 100 kPa).
         </div>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr style="background:#f8eaba; border-top:2px solid transparent;">
       <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="525" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/12px-X_mark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/18px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/24px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" width="12"/>
        <span style="display:none">
         N
        </span>
        <span class="reflink plainlinks nourlexpansion">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:ComparePages&amp;rev1=411004179&amp;page2=N-Butanol">
          verify
         </a>
        </span>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Chemicals/Chembox_validation" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Chemicals/Chembox validation">
         what is
        </a>
        <sup>
         <img alt="Yes" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="7" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/7px-Yes_check.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/11px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/14px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" width="7"/>
         <span style="display:none">
          Y
         </span>
         <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="525" height="8" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/7px-X_mark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/11px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/14px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" width="7"/>
         <span style="display:none">
          N
         </span>
        </sup>
        ?)
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr style="background:#f8eaba; border-top:2px solid transparent;">
       <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;">
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Chemical_infobox#References" title="Wikipedia:Chemical infobox">
         Infobox references
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr style="background:#f8eaba;">
       <td style="width:40%; max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-right:1px solid transparent;">
       </td>
       <td style="width:60%; max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-left:1px solid transparent;">
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       -Butanol
      </b>
      or
      <b>
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       -butyl alcohol
      </b>
      or
      <b>
       normal butanol
      </b>
      is a primary
      <a href="/wiki/Alcohol" title="Alcohol">
       alcohol
      </a>
      with a 4-
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">
       carbon
      </a>
      structure and the
      <a href="/wiki/Chemical_formula" title="Chemical formula">
       chemical formula
      </a>
      C
      <sub>
       4
      </sub>
      H
      <sub>
       9
      </sub>
      OH. Its
      <a href="/wiki/Isomer" title="Isomer">
       isomers
      </a>
      include
      <a href="/wiki/Isobutanol" title="Isobutanol">
       isobutanol
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/2-Butanol" title="2-Butanol">
       2-butanol
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tert-Butanol" title="Tert-Butanol">
       <i>
        tert
       </i>
       -butanol
      </a>
      . Butanol is one of the group of "
      <a href="/wiki/Fusel_alcohol" title="Fusel alcohol">
       fusel alcohols
      </a>
      " (from the German for "bad liquor"), which have more than two carbon atoms and have significant solubility in water.
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol occurs naturally as a minor product of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fermentation" title="Ethanol fermentation">
       fermentation
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">
       sugars
      </a>
      and other
      <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">
       carbohydrates
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is present in many foods and beverages.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHC_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EHC-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also a permitted artificial flavorant in the United States,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
      used in butter, cream, fruit, rum, whiskey, ice cream and ices, candy, baked goods and cordials.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also used in a wide range of consumer products.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHC_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-EHC-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The largest use of
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol is as an industrial intermediate, particularly for the manufacture of
      <a href="/wiki/Butyl_acetate" title="Butyl acetate">
       butyl acetate
      </a>
      (itself an artificial flavorant and industrial solvent). It is a
      <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">
       petrochemical
      </a>
      , manufactured from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propylene" title="Propylene">
       propylene
      </a>
      and usually used close to the point of manufacture. Estimated production figures for 1997 are: United States 784,000 tonnes; Western Europe 575,000 tonnes; Japan 225,000 tonnes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">
       Production
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Production">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is produced industrially from the petrochemical feedstock
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propylene" title="Propylene">
       propylene
      </a>
      . Propylene is
      <a href="/wiki/Hydroformylation" title="Hydroformylation">
       hydroformylated
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Butyraldehyde" title="Butyraldehyde">
       butyraldehyde
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxo_process" title="Oxo process">
       oxo process
      </a>
      ) in the presence of a
      <a href="/wiki/Rhodium" title="Rhodium">
       rhodium
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Homogeneous_catalysis" title="Homogeneous catalysis">
       homogeneous catalyst
      </a>
      similar to
      <a href="/wiki/Wilkinson%27s_catalyst" title="Wilkinson's catalyst">
       Wilkinson's catalyst
      </a>
      . The butyraldehyde is then
      <a href="/wiki/Hydrogenation" title="Hydrogenation">
       hydrogenated
      </a>
      to produce
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_use">
       Industrial use
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Industrial use">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol is an intermediate in the production of
      <a href="/wiki/Butyl_acrylate" title="Butyl acrylate">
       butyl acrylate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Butyl_acetate" title="Butyl acetate">
       butyl acetate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dibutyl_phthalate" title="Dibutyl phthalate">
       dibutyl phthalate
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dibutyl_sebacate" title="Dibutyl sebacate">
       dibutyl sebacate
      </a>
      , and other butyl esters,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mellan_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mellan-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doolittle_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Doolittle-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      butyl ethers such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethylene_glycol_monobutyl_ether" title="Ethylene glycol monobutyl ether">
       ethylene glycol monobutyl ether
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Diethylene_glycol_monobutyl_ether&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Diethylene glycol monobutyl ether (page does not exist)">
       di-
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Triethylene_glycol_monobutyl_ether&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Triethylene glycol monobutyl ether (page does not exist)">
       triethylene glycol monobutyl ether
      </a>
      , and the corresponding butyl ether acetates. Other industrial uses include the manufacture of pharmaceuticals, polymers,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyroxylin" title="Pyroxylin">
       pyroxylin
      </a>
      plastics, herbicide esters, printing (e.g.,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2,4-D" title="2,4-D">
       2,4-D
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2,4,5-T" title="2,4,5-T">
       2,4,5-T
      </a>
      )
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monich_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Monich-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Butyl_xanthate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Butyl xanthate (page does not exist)">
       butyl xanthate
      </a>
      . It is also used as a diluent/reactant in the manufacture of
      <a href="/wiki/Urea" title="Urea">
       urea
      </a>
      –
      <a href="/wiki/Formaldehyde" title="Formaldehyde">
       formaldehyde
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Melamine" title="Melamine">
       melamine
      </a>
      –formaldehyde resins.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_uses">
       Other uses
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Other uses">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is used as an ingredient in perfumes and as a solvent for the extraction of
      <a href="/wiki/Essential_oil" title="Essential oil">
       essential oils
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mellan_11-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mellan-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is also used as an extractant in the manufacture of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">
       antibiotics
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hormone" title="Hormone">
       hormones
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">
       vitamins
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mellan_11-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mellan-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doolittle_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Doolittle-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      a solvent for paints, coatings, natural resins, gums, synthetic resins, dyes,
      <a href="/wiki/Alkaloid" title="Alkaloid">
       alkaloids
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Camphor" title="Camphor">
       camphor
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mellan_11-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mellan-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doolittle_12-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Doolittle-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other miscellaneous applications of
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol are as a swelling agent in textiles, as a component of hydraulic
      <a href="/wiki/Brake_fluid" title="Brake fluid">
       brake fluids
      </a>
      , cleaning formulations,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degreaser" title="Degreaser">
       degreasers
      </a>
      , and repellents;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHC_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-EHC-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and as a component of ore floation agents,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monich_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Monich-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and of wood-treating systems.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol has been proposed
      <a href="/wiki/Butanol_fuel" title="Butanol fuel">
       as a substitute
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">
       diesel fuel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">
       gasoline
      </a>
      . It is produced in small quantities in nearly all
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(biochemistry)" title="Fermentation (biochemistry)">
       fermentations
      </a>
      (see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fusel_oil" title="Fusel oil">
       fusel oil
      </a>
      ), but species of
      <a href="/wiki/Clostridium" title="Clostridium">
       Clostridium
      </a>
      produce much higher yields of butanol, and research is currently underway to increase the ultimate yield of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biobutanol" title="Biobutanol">
       biobutanol
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">
       biomass
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The production or, in some cases, use of the following substances may result in exposure to
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol:
      <a href="/wiki/Artificial_leather" title="Artificial leather">
       artificial leather
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Butyl_ester" title="Butyl ester">
       butyl esters
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rubber_cement" title="Rubber cement">
       rubber cement
      </a>
      , dyes, fruit essences, lacquers, motion picture, and photographic films, raincoats, perfumes,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyroxylin" title="Pyroxylin">
       pyroxylin
      </a>
      plastics,
      <a href="/wiki/Rayon" title="Rayon">
       rayon
      </a>
      , safety glass,
      <a href="/wiki/Shellac" title="Shellac">
       shellac
      </a>
      varnish, and waterproofed cloth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHC_7-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-EHC-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence_in_Nature">
       Occurrence in Nature
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Occurrence in Nature">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Honey_bee" title="Honey bee">
       Honey bees
      </a>
      use n-butanol as an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alarm_pheromone" title="Alarm pheromone">
       Alarm pheromone
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence_in_food">
       Occurrence in food
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Occurrence in food">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol occurs naturally as a result of carbohydrate fermentation in a number of alcoholic beverages, including beer,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      grape brandies,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
      wine,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and whisky.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It has been detected in the volatiles of hops,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      jack fruit,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
      heat-treated milks,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        [21]
       </a>
      </sup>
      musk melon,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        [22]
       </a>
      </sup>
      cheese,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
      southern pea seed,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and cooked rice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is also formed during deep frying of corn oil, cottonseed oil, trilinolein, and triolein.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is used as an ingredient in processed and artificial flavourings,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mellan_11-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mellan-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and for the extraction of lipid-free protein from egg yolk,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      natural flavouring materials and vegetable oils, the manufacture of hop extract for beermaking, and as a solvent in removing pigments from moist curd
      <a href="/wiki/Leaf_protein_concentrate" title="Leaf protein concentrate">
       leaf protein concentrate
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Metabolism_and_toxicity">
       Metabolism and toxicity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Metabolism and toxicity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is readily absorbed through the intestinal tract and lungs, and also to some extent through the skin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is metabolized completely in vertebrates in a manner similar to
      <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">
       ethanol
      </a>
      :
      <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_dehydrogenase" title="Alcohol dehydrogenase">
       alcohol dehydrogenase
      </a>
      converts
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol to
      <a href="/wiki/Butyraldehyde" title="Butyraldehyde">
       butyraldehyde
      </a>
      ; this is then converted to
      <a href="/wiki/Butyric_acid" title="Butyric acid">
       butyric acid
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Aldehyde_dehydrogenase" title="Aldehyde dehydrogenase">
       aldehyde dehydrogenase
      </a>
      . Butyric acid can be fully metabolized to
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">
       carbon dioxide
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">
       water
      </a>
      by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%92-oxidation" title="Β-oxidation">
       β-oxidation
      </a>
      pathway. In the rat, only 0.03% of an oral dose of 2000 mg/kg was excreted in the urine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The acute toxicity of
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol is relatively low, with oral
      <a href="/wiki/Median_lethal_dose" title="Median lethal dose">
       LD
       <sub>
        50
       </sub>
      </a>
      values of 790–4360 mg/kg (rat; comparable values for ethanol are 7000–15000 mg/kg).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
      No deaths were reported at an inhaled concentration of 8000 ppm (4-hour exposure, rats). At sub-lethal doses,
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol acts as a
      <a href="/wiki/Depressant" title="Depressant">
       depressant
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">
       central nervous system
      </a>
      , similar to ethanol: one study in rats indicated that the intoxicating potency of
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol is some six times higher than that of ethanol, possibly because of its slower transformation by alcohol dehydrogenase.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is a natural component of many alcoholic beverages, albeit in low (but variable) concentrations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It (along with similar
      <a href="/wiki/Fusel_alcohol" title="Fusel alcohol">
       fusel alcohols
      </a>
      ) is reputed to be responsible for severe "
      <a href="/wiki/Hangover" title="Hangover">
       hangovers
      </a>
      ", although experiments in animal models show no evidence for this.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
      An unknown dose
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol was consumed by a 47-year-old male with no previous medical history, leading to a range of adverse health effects.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_hazards">
       Other hazards
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=N-Butanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other hazards">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Liquid
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol, as is common with most organic solvents, is extremely irritating to the eyes; repeated contact with the skin can also cause irritation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is believed to be a generic effect of "defatting". No skin sensitization has been observed. Irritation of the respiratory pathways occurs only at very high concentrations (&gt;2400 ppm).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monell_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Monell-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With a
      <a href="/wiki/Flash_point" title="Flash point">
       flash point
      </a>
      of 35 °C,
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol presents a moderate fire hazard: it is slightly more flammable than
      <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">
       kerosene
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">
       diesel fuel
      </a>
      but less flammable than many other common organic solvents. The depressant effect on the central nervous system (similar to ethanol intoxication) is a potential hazard when working with
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -butanol in enclosed spaces, although the odour threshold (0.2–30 ppm) is far below the concentration which would have any neurological effect.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monell_37-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Monell-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       n
      </i>
      -Butanol is of low toxicity to aquatic vertebrates and invertebrates. It is rapidly biodegraded in water, although an estimated 83% partitions to air where it is degraded by
      <a href="/wiki/Hydroxyl_radical" title="Hydroxyl radical">
       hydroxyl radicals
      </a>
      with a half-life of 1.2–2.3 days. It has low potential to
      <a href="/wiki/Bioaccumulation" title="Bioaccumulation">
       bioaccumulate
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIDS_8-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-SIDS-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A potential hazard of significant discharges to watercourses is the rise in
      <a href="/wiki/Chemical_oxygen_demand" title="Chemical oxygen demand">
       chemical oxygen demand
      </a>
      (C.O.D.) associated with its biodegradation.
     </p>

         .
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-EHC-7">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-EHC_7-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
